< review>
Second time coming here in a few years since they took over the previous Mexican restaurant that was here I think it was called Las Palmas.

First time I ordered burritos here and the food was just okay because the rice in the burrito was hard like it was undercooked and thought that maybe it was a one time thing and I was just not lucky that day.

This second time visiting I ordered burritos and "super tacos". There was nothing super about the tacos.  Two pieces of very dry tortillas that was on the grill top too long with a bit of cheese and topped with very dry salty Carne asada. That's it. Nothing super about that taco. Was expecting fluffy tortillas with juicy beef and some onions cilantro and maybe tomatoes with a hint of lime. Nope.. The burritos I ordered were "wet burritos" which is a burrito in a red sauce which I think it is enchilada sauce? First burrito was carne asada and second was al pastor (pork). Both burritos were generous sized and filling but the rice was hard and undercooked.  The Carne asada filling was dry and salty. The al pastor pork meat was better but a bit flavorless. There was very minimal salsa in the burritos so it was a bit in the dry side.  The beans inside were good though,  I liked them.  The red enchilada sauce that makes it a "wet burrito" was just too salty which hid the flavors of all the ingredients in that sauce.

I gave the review 3 stars only because the food i got was just a bit less than okay but the staff was really nice.  I'm sure there must be other food there that might be better tasting.<//review>

<username>P. I.<//username><Date>1535234342250<//Date><Rate>3<//Rate>< Review>
Great standby Salvadorian mexican restaurant ,  with traditional tasting Pupusas, and straight ahead tacos, served in a family setting, often with catholic services on the large screen TV, reminding you to tip well or face the wrath of God. If you've never had a pupusa, get a beef one, and marvel at what can only be described as a savory stuffed tortilla, served with a sauce similar to coleslaw, called, "Curtido" (Pickled Cole Slaw) in a red salsa. The food has been a little hit or miss sometimes, but still tasty.<//Review>

<time>1516515334274</time>< text>
I love the pupusas rebueltas (mixed carnitas/beans/cheese) and pupusas zucchini/cheese. I've tried the pupusas at several other places, and I like these best - the innards are mixed well, are seasoned well, and the tortillas portion is just slightly silky to the tongue. The cabbage salsa that comes with them is awesome and sometimes has different types of cabbage in it. I've had these in the restaurant and to go, it's great both ways (the paper plate to go sometimes doesn't hold up against the cutting because of  the steaming). Sometimes the tomato sauce is mixed in with the cabbage, which works okay. I also like the carne asada street tacos served with radishes and lime wedges.< /text>

I went here ages ago for a burrito, and decided that Chipotle or Gordos was a better option.

Just went back for Pupusas awhile ago, and was stunned.  This place has*great* pupusas!!

Have been back 3x since.  Always great.

2 caveats: they make the pupusas while you wait, and I've generally waited~15 mins when ordering 4-6.  (Drank a horchata while waiting.  Yum!)

2nd point -- the venue is full of local color.  Try not to judge the food by the variety of folk coming in for a bite.  I've seen homeless folks, poor folks, and working class galore.</text>

<user_id>112063491834906835067</user_id><username>WOLVERINE S<//username>< date>
1363719599625< /date>
<rating>5<//rating>< review>
I was at the March 2013 auction and got a great deal.  I have been at city auctions, which you basically bid on cars that you dont know what you are getting to.  On these auctions you have to buy very low, because you will need extra cash for repairs or maybe not if you get very lucky.  This past March it was my first time at General Auction, and the bidding here is different.  You are pretty much bidding on cars that in great conditions and smog certified prior to putting them at the auction.

Just remember that you are not bidding on at city auction, these cars or at least most of them are in very good conditions.  Otherwise you are told about them.

The vehicles that are for dealers or dismantlers are vehicles that have been in very serious accidents or require mechanical or body repairs.  You can find those type of cars at city auctions, if you want to go through the hassle of reparing.

My props for their staff.  I had a minor issue and gave them a call explaining them my issue.  They asked me to come in to review and discuss the issue further.  I came in the following day and spoke with the General manager, a great guy.  He doesnt BS you, he tells you how it is and offer to help you out.  They dont just take your money and look the other way, if any issues they are willing to help you resolve it.  Long story short my issue was resolved.

How great of a deal was the car I bought:

The vehicle I bought had LOTTTTS of miles on it, and I was able to sell it within 7 days and made good profit.  Everything in this car was almost new.  The buyer was a mechanic and knew right away that he was getting a steal from me.

I guess I got a steal from General Auction.

See you guys in April!!!!!!<//review>

<rate>5< /rate>< Text>
SOOOO SAD they're going out of business! Prices are too high. Maybe that's why--can't compete with Target and Wal-Mart (and all of the online sites to buy toys), but there's nothing like going to Toys-R-Us for a child. It's magical, and worth the few extra bucks. We went 3 days ago, and the whole store was 10-30% off (mostly 10% off) which made the cost of our purchase almost comparable to the competitors. I'll be bringing my daughter a couple times a week until they're closed. They're the only toy store that has their mascot (Geoffrey the Giraffe) call children on their birthday with happy birthday wishes & send a $3 birthday card/coupon. We will miss Toys-R-Us. When I was growing up, it was THE place to get your first bike, your Barbies, and Cabbage Patch dolls. I guess kids get their bikes at Wal-Mart now. It's a shame. There's no more large toy stores--retail stores just for kids--anymore. Sad. Growing up, there were toy stores in malls too. I guess the online generation will get their toys online now too...I think it sucks.</Text>
